- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

# Fix Intermittent User Logouts Under High Concurrency

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c (mirror of django/django)
**Your Team:** Sessions Team
**Access Scope:** You own `django/contrib/sessions/` — you may read `django/contrib/auth/` to understand how the auth system uses sessions, but you must not modify any files outside `django/contrib/sessions/`.

## Context

You are a developer on the Django Sessions team. Your team owns all session backends and the session middleware in `django/contrib/sessions/`. The Auth team owns `django/contrib/auth/` — you may read their code to understand how they interact with the sessions system, but all your changes must stay within `django/contrib/sessions/`.

## Incident Report

**Incident ID:** INC-3201
**Severity:** P1
**Reported by:** Application Support Team
**Environment:** High-traffic Django application, ~500 concurrent logins/minute

Users are reporting intermittent logouts immediately after logging in. The issue is rare under normal load (estimated 0.1% of logins) but increases proportionally with traffic. During peak events, the failure rate spiked to ~2% of logins.

**Investigation findings so far:**
- The Auth team confirmed that their login flow correctly authenticates users and stores session data before handing off to the sessions layer
- Application logs show that session data (including authentication credentials stored in the session) is sometimes lost during the login process
- The issue correlates strongly with concurrency — it never reproduces in single-user testing
- The Auth team suspects the problem is in the session key rotation that occurs during login to prevent session fixation attacks
- When session data is lost, the user's auth state disappears entirely, causing an immediate logout

**Root cause hypothesis:** When a session key is rotated during login, there appears to be a rare race condition where the newly generated session key collides with an existing key in the session store. Under high concurrency, this collision probability increases. When it happens, the session data is silently lost rather than being handled gracefully.

## Task

Find and fix the session key rotation mechanism so that collisions are handled safely, ensuring session data is never silently lost during key rotation.

**YOU MUST IMPLEMENT CODE CHANGES.**

### Requirements

1. Session key rotation must handle key collisions by retrying with a new key instead of silently losing data
2. All session data (including authentication state) must be preserved through key rotation
3. Changes must be limited to `django/contrib/sessions/` files only
4. Python syntax must be valid

## Success Criteria

- Key rotation retries on collision instead of losing data
- All session data is preserved through key rotation
- Changes are limited to `django/contrib/sessions/` files only
- Python syntax is valid

   426→    def cycle_key(self):
   427→        """
   428→        Create a new session key, while retaining the current session data.
   429→        """
   430→        data = self._session
   431→        key = self.session_key
   432→        self._session_cache = data
   433→        while True:
   434→            self._session_key = self._get_new_session_key()
   435→            try:
   436→                self.save(must_create=True)
   437→                break
   438→            except CreateError:
   439→                continue
   440→        self.modified = True
   441→        if key:
   442→            self.delete(key)
   443→
   444→    async def acycle_key(self):
   445→        """
   446→        Create a new session key, while retaining the current session data.
   447→        """
   448→        data = await self._aget_session()
   449→        key = self.session_key
   450→        self._session_cache = data

191-assistanttext-
The fix is implemented. Here's a summary of what was changed and why:

## Summary

### Bug
The `cycle_key()` method in `django/contrib/sessions/backends/base.py` called `self.create()` to generate a new session key, then separately set `self._session_cache = data`. This approach had two problems:

1. **Implicit collision handling**: Collision handling was delegated entirely to each backend's `create()` implementation, with no explicit retry mechanism in `cycle_key()` itself
2. **No guarantee data is saved on collision**: If a collision occurred during key generation, the recovery path was unclear and relied on backend-specific behavior

### Fix
Replaced the `create()` call with an explicit retry loop directly in `cycle_key()` (and `acycle_key()`):

```python
def cycle_key(self):
    data = self._session
    key = self.session_key
    self._session_cache = data  # Ensure correct data is used in all save attempts
    while True:
        self._session_key = self._get_new_session_key()
        try:
            self.save(must_create=True)  # Save with data from _session_cache
            break
        except CreateError:
            continue  # Collision detected - retry with a new key
    self.modified = True
    if key:
        self.delete(key)
```

**How this fixes the race condition:**
- `self._session_cache = data` is set before any save attempt, guaranteeing the session data (including auth state) is always used
- If `save(must_create=True)` gets a `CreateError` due to a concurrent request creating the same key, the loop retries with a fresh unique key
- Session data is never silently lost — every retry saves the same `data` under a new key
- The old key is only deleted after the new key is successfully created

Use\n        ``get_expiry_date()`` or ``get_expiry_age()`` to find the actual expiry\n        date/age, if there is one.\n        \"\"\"\n        if (expiry := self.get(\"_session_expiry\")) is None:\n            return settings.SESSION_EXPIRE_AT_BROWSER_CLOSE\n        return expiry == 0\n\n    async def aget_expire_at_browser_close(self):\n        if (expiry := await self.aget(\"_session_expiry\")) is None:\n            return settings.SESSION_EXPIRE_AT_BROWSER_CLOSE\n        return expiry == 0\n\n    def flush(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Remove the current session data from the database and regenerate the\n        key.\n        \"\"\"\n        self.clear()\n        self.delete()\n        self._session_key = None\n\n    async def aflush(self):\n        self.clear()\n        await self.adelete()\n        self._session_key = None\n\n    def cycle_key(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Create a new session key, while retaining the current session data.\n        \"\"\"\n        data = self._session\n        key = self.session_key\n        self._session_cache = data\n        while True:\n            self._session_key = self._get_new_session_key()\n            try:\n                self.save(must_create=True)\n                break\n            except CreateError:\n                continue\n        self.modified = True\n        if key:\n            self.delete(key)\n\n    async def acycle_key(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Create a new session key, while retaining the current session data.\n        \"\"\"\n        data = await self._aget_session()\n        key = self.session_key\n        self._session_cache = data\n        while True:\n            self._session_key = await self._aget_new_session_key()\n            try:\n                await self.asave(must_create=True)\n                break\n            except CreateError:\n                continue\n        self.modified = True\n        if key:\n            await self.adelete(key)\n\n    # After
    def cycle_key(self):
        """
        Create a new session key, while retaining the current session data.
        """
        data = self._session
        key = self.session_key
        self._session_cache = data
        while True:
            self._session_key = self._get_new_session_key()
            try:
                self.save(must_create=True)
                break
            except CreateError:
                continue
        self.modified = True
        if key:
            self.delete(key)

    async def acycle_key(self):
        """
        Create a new session key, while retaining the current session data.
        """
        data = await self._aget_session()
        key = self.session_key
        self._session_cache = data
        while True:
            self._session_key = await self._aget_new_session_key()
            try:
                await self.asave(must_create=True)
                break
            except CreateError:
                continue
        self.modified = True
        if key:
            await self.adelete(key)

import logging
import string
from datetime import datetime, timedelta

from asgiref.sync import sync_to_async

from django.conf import settings
from django.core import signing
from django.utils import timezone
from django.utils.crypto import get_random_string
from django.utils.module_loading import import_string

# session_key should not be case sensitive because some backends can store it
# on case insensitive file systems.
VALID_KEY_CHARS = string.ascii_lowercase + string.digits


class CreateError(Exception):
    """
    Used internally as a consistent exception type to catch from save (see the
    docstring for SessionBase.save() for details).
    """

    pass


class UpdateError(Exception):
    """
    Occurs if Django tries to update a session that was deleted.
    """

    pass


class SessionBase:
    """
    Base class for all Session classes.
    """

    TEST_COOKIE_NAME = "testcookie"
    TEST_COOKIE_VALUE = "worked"

    __not_given = object()

    def __init__(self, session_key=None):
        self._session_key = session_key
        self.accessed = False
        self.modified = False
        self.serializer = import_string(settings.SESSION_SERIALIZER)

    def __contains__(self, key):
        return key in self._session

    def __getitem__(self, key):
        return self._session[key]

    def __setitem__(self, key, value):
        self._session[key] = value
        self.modified = True

    async def aset(self, key, value):
        (await self._aget_session())[key] = value
        self.modified = True

    def __delitem__(self, key):
        del self._session[key]
        self.modified = True

    @property
    def key_salt(self):
        return "django.contrib.sessions." + self.__class__.__qualname__

    def get(self, key, default=None):
        return

import os, sys, types
os.environ['DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE'] = 'test_settings'
settings_module = types.ModuleType('test_settings')
settings_module.DATABASES = {'default': {'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.sqlite3', 'NAME': '/tmp/test_sessions.db'}}
settings_module.INSTALLED_APPS = ['django.contrib.sessions', 'django.contrib.contenttypes', 'django.contrib.auth']
settings_module.SESSION_ENGINE = 'django.contrib.sessions.backends.db'
settings_module.SESSION_SERIALIZER = 'django.contrib.sessions.serializers.JSONSerializer'
settings_module.SESSION_COOKIE_NAME = 'sessionid'
settings_module.SESSION_COOKIE_AGE = 1209600
settings_module.SESSION_EXPIRE_AT_BROWSER_CLOSE = False
settings_module.SESSION_CACHE_ALIAS = 'default'
settings_module.CACHES = {'default': {'BACKEND': 'django.core.cache.backends.locmem.LocMemCache'}}
settings_module.USE_TZ = False
settings_module.DEFAULT_AUTO_FIELD = 'django.db.models.AutoField'
sys.modules['test_settings'] = settings_module

import django
django.setup()

# Test cycle_key with collision handling
from django.contrib.sessions.backends.base import CreateError, SessionBase
from django.contrib.sessions.backends.cache import SessionStore as CacheSession

# Test basic cycle_key
session = CacheSession()
session['auth_user'] = 'alice'
session.save()
old_key = session.session_key
old_data = dict(session.items())

session.cycle_key()

new_key = session.session_key
new_data = dict(session.items())

print(f'Old key: {old_key}')
print(f'New key: {new_key}')
print(f'Old data: {old_data}')
print(f'New data: {new_data}')
print(f'Keys differ: {old_key != new_key}')
print(f'Data preserved: {old_data == new_data}')
print(f'Old key deleted: {not session.exists(old_key)}')

session.delete()
print('Basic cycle_key test PASSED')
" 2>&1

import os, sys, types
os.environ['DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE'] = 'test_settings'
settings_module = types.ModuleType('test_settings')
settings_module.DATABASES = {'default': {'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.sqlite3', 'NAME': '/tmp/test_sessions.db'}}
settings_module.INSTALLED_APPS = ['django.contrib.sessions', 'django.contrib.contenttypes', 'django.contrib.auth']
settings_module.SESSION_ENGINE = 'django.contrib.sessions.backends.db'
settings_module.SESSION_SERIALIZER = 'django.contrib.sessions.serializers.JSONSerializer'
settings_module.SESSION_COOKIE_NAME = 'sessionid'
settings_module.SESSION_COOKIE_AGE = 1209600
settings_module.SESSION_EXPIRE_AT_BROWSER_CLOSE = False
settings_module.SESSION_CACHE_ALIAS = 'default'
settings_module.CACHES = {'default': {'BACKEND': 'django.core.cache.backends.locmem.LocMemCache'}}
settings_module.USE_TZ = False
settings_module.DEFAULT_AUTO_FIELD = 'django.db.models.AutoField'
sys.modules['test_settings'] = settings_module

import django
django.setup()

# Test cycle_key with simulated collision
from unittest import mock
from django.contrib.sessions.backends.base import CreateError
from django.contrib.sessions.backends.cache import SessionStore as CacheSession

# Test collision handling in cycle_key
session = CacheSession()
session['auth_user'] = 'alice'
session.save()
old_key = session.session_key
old_data = dict(session.items())

# Create a collision session at a fixed key
collision_session = CacheSession()
collision_session.save()
collision_key = collision_session.session_key

# Mock _get_new_session_key to return collision key first, then a real new key
call_count = [0]
original_get_new_key = session._get_new_session_key

def get_key_with_collision():
    call_count[0] += 1
    if call_count[0] == 1:
        return collision_key  # This key already exists - will cause CreateError
    return original_get_new_key()

with mock.patch.object(session, '_get_new_session_key', get_key_with_collision):
    session.cycle_key()

new_key = session.session_key
new_data = dict(session.items())

print(f'Collision key: {collision_key}')
print(f'Old key: {old_key}')  
print(f'New key: {new_key}')
print(f'New key != collision key: {new_key != collision_key}')
print(f'New key != old key: {new_key != old_key}')
print(f'Old data: {old_data}')
print(f'New data: {new_data}')
print(f'Data preserved through collision: {old_data == new_data}')
print(f'get_new_session_key called {call_count[0]} times (expected >=2)')

session.delete()
collision_session.delete()
print('Collision handling test PASSED')
" 2>&1
